
  <article class="pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer--css-not-removed"> 
   <script>
      'use strict';

            var $outerWrapper = document.querySelector('.pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer');
      if ($outerWrapper && $outerWrapper.closest) {
        var $containerWrapper = $outerWrapper.closest('.container');
        if ($containerWrapper) {
          $containerWrapper.classList.remove('container');
          $containerWrapper.classList.add('j-chrome-content-container');
        }
      }

            var cssRemoved = false;
      try {
        var $crapCss = document.querySelectorAll(
          'link[href*="/chrome_themes/nimbus/css/pages.css"], link[href*="/chrome_themes/nimbus/css/components.css"]'
        );
        if ($crapCss.length) {
          for (let index = 0; index < $crapCss.length; index++) {
            const $stylesheet = $crapCss[index];
            $stylesheet.remove();
          }
        }
        cssRemoved = true;
      }
      catch (error) {
        console.error('Ran into an issue while trying to retheme page', error);
        cssRemoved = false;
      }

            if (cssRemoved) {
        var $pvofOuterWrapper = document.querySelector('.pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer--css-not-removed');
        if ($pvofOuterWrapper) {
          $pvofOuterWrapper.classList.remove('pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer--css-not-removed');
        }
      }
    </script>

     <div class="doc-wrapper pvof-doc__wrapper j-superdoc__content-wrapper" id="doc-wrapper"> 
      <div class="pane-page-title"> 
       <h1 class="title" itemprop="name">Release Notes for Red Hat Fuse 7.9</h1> 
      </div> 
      <div xml:lang="en-US" class="book" id="idm140679273400048">
       <div class="titlepage">
        <div>
         <div class="producttitle">
          <span class="productname">Red Hat Fuse</span> <span class="productnumber">7.9</span>
         </div>
         <div>
          <h2 class="subtitle">What's new in Red Hat Fuse</h2>
         </div>
         <div>
          <div xml:lang="en-US" class="authorgroup">
           <span class="org"> <span class="orgname">Red Hat Fuse Documentation Team</span> </span>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div>
          <a href="#idm140679319079504">Legal Notice</a>
         </div>
         <div>
          <div class="abstract">
           <p class="title"><strong>Abstract</strong></p>
           <div class="para">
             These notes provide an overview of the changes between Red Hat Fuse releases. 
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <hr>
       </div>
       <section class="preface" id="making-open-source-more-inclusive">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Making open source more inclusive</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> Red Hat is committed to replacing problematic language in our code, documentation, and web properties. We are beginning with these four terms: master, slave, blacklist, and whitelist. Because of the enormity of this endeavor, these changes will be implemented gradually over several upcoming releases. For more details, see our <a class="link" href="https://www.redhat.com/en/blog/making-open-source-more-inclusive-eradicating-problematic-language">CTO Chris Wright’s message</a>. </p>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="Product">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;1.&nbsp;Fuse 7.9 Product Overview</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <section class="section" id="Product-Distributions">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">1.1.&nbsp;Fuse distributions</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse 7.9 is provided in the form of three different distributions, as follows: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse standalone</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The classic distribution of Fuse, supported on multiple operating systems. This distribution is supported for the following container types: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
              <li class="listitem"> Apache Karaf </li>
              <li class="listitem"> JBoss Enterprise Application Platform (EAP) </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Spring Boot </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse on OpenShift</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The distribution of Fuse for running integration applications on OpenShift (supported on the Red Hat Enterprise Linux operating system). In this case, the supported container types are provided in the form of docker-formatted container images: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
              <li class="listitem"> Java image (for Spring Boot) </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Apache Karaf image </li>
              <li class="listitem"> JBoss EAP image </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse Online</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The distribution of Fuse for non-expert integrators with a simplified workflow accessed through a browser based UI. This distribution is available for the following kinds of deployment: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
              <li class="listitem"> On an OpenShift Dedicated (OSD) cluster. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> For installation on an on-premises OpenShift cluster </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="Product-New">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">1.2.&nbsp;New features</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse 7.9 includes several major component upgrades and a large selection of new features. For details, consult the <span class="emphasis"><em>new features</em></span> sections for each of the Fuse distributions: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="#OnlineDistrib-Features" title="2.2.&nbsp;New features in Fuse Online 7.9">New features for Fuse Online</a> </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="#FISDistrib-Features" title="3.3.&nbsp;New features in Fuse 7.9 on OpenShift">New features for Fuse on OpenShift</a> </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="#StandaloneDistrib-Features" title="4.2.&nbsp;New features in Fuse 7.9">New features for Fuse standalone</a> </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="SupportedConfigurations">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">1.3.&nbsp;Supported Configurations</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="admonition important">
          <div class="admonition_header">
           Important
          </div>
          <div>
           <p> For running Fuse in Apache Karaf, we recommend OpenJDK 8u282 or OpenJDK 8u302. Do not use OpenJDK 8u292, which has a known issue affecting the credential store (see <a class="link" href="#known-issue-entesb-16417">ENTESB-16417</a>). OracleJDK 1.8.0_291 is also affected by this issue. </p>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> For information about supported configurations, standards, and components in version 7.9, see the following Customer Portal articles: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/articles/310603">Red Hat Fuse Supported Configurations</a> </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/articles/375743">Red Hat Fuse Supported Standards</a> </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/articles/348423">Red Hat Fuse Component Details</a> </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="OnlineDistrib">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;2.&nbsp;Fuse Online</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> Fuse Online provides a web browser interface that lets a business expert integrate two or more different applications or services without writing code. It also provides features that allow the addition of code if it is needed for complex use cases. </p>
        <p> Fuse Online runs an integration on OpenShift as a Spring Boot application that uses Apache Camel. </p>
        <section class="section" id="about-fuse-online-distributions">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.1.&nbsp;About Fuse Online distributions</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse Online is Red Hat’s web-based integration platform. <a class="link" href="https://github.com/syndesisio/syndesis">Syndesis</a> is the open source project for Fuse Online. Fuse Online runs in these OpenShift environments: </p>
         <div class="informaltable">
          <table class="lt-4-cols lt-7-rows">
           <colgroup>
            <col style="width: 50%; " class="col_1"><!--Empty-->
           </colgroup>
           <colgroup>
            <col style="width: 50%; " class="col_2"><!--Empty-->
           </colgroup>
           <tbody>
            <tr>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Host Environment</strong></span> </p> </td>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Installation</strong></span> </p> </td>
            </tr>
            <tr>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> OpenShift Dedicated </p> </td>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> Red Hat installs and provisions Fuse Online on Red Hat infrastructure. </p> </td>
            </tr>
            <tr>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> OpenShift Container Platform </p> </td>
             <td align="left" valign="top"> <p> Customer installs and manages. </p> </td>
            </tr>
           </tbody>
          </table>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="OnlineDistrib-Features">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.2.&nbsp;New features in Fuse Online 7.9</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse Online 7.9 provides the following new features: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>SOAP API client connector</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> You can add a custom SOAP API client connector and then add a connection for a SOAP API client to Fuse Online integrations. For more information, see <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/integrating_applications_with_fuse_online/index#creating-soap-api-connectors_add-client-connector">Creating SOAP API client connectors</a>. </p><p class="simpara"> This release of the SOAP API client connector has some limitations as described in the <a class="link" href="#known-issues-fuse-online" title="7.2.&nbsp;Fuse Online">Fuse Online</a> section of Important Notes for Fuse Online. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>New data mapper features</strong></span> </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="circle">
              <li class="listitem"> Support for a new conditional expression. For a collection with multiple fields, the data mapper can now filter the values in one source field based on the value of a different source field (in the same collection). </li>
              <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> Support for two new transformations: </p>
               <div class="itemizedlist">
                <ul class="itemizedlist" type="square">
                 <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">CopyTo</code> Copies the value of a source string field into a specified field of a target collection without splitting. </li>
                 <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">Repeat</code> When mapping a simple type to an array type, fills multiple array fields with the value taken from the simple type. </li>
                </ul>
               </div></li>
              <li class="listitem"> In the data mapper UI, XML attributes are now indicated by the @ symbol. </li>
              <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> The Fuse Online 7.9 data mapper is upgraded from AtlasMap 2.0.0 to 2.2.2. For details about the bug fixes and minor enhancements in version 2.2.2, see the following upstream AtlasMap release notes: </p><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.1.1">https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.1.1</a> </p><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.1.2">https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.1.2</a> </p><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.0">https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.0</a> </p><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.1">https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.1</a> </p><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.2">https://github.com/atlasmap/atlasmap/releases/tag/atlasmap-2.2.2</a> </p></li>
             </ul>
            </div></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>FTP connector actions</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> In previous releases, the FTP connector had two actions (<code class="literal">Download</code> and <code class="literal">Upload</code>). Starting with Fuse Online 7.9, there are two additional actions for an FTP server: <code class="literal">DownloadNamedFile</code> and <code class="literal">UploadNamedFile</code>. Also, for the <span class="strong strong"><strong>file name expression</strong></span>, you now provide an <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_camel_development_guide/index#file">Apache Camel File language</a> expression to specify the file or files to download or upload. </p></li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="changes_in_fuse_online_7_9">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.3.&nbsp;Changes in Fuse Online 7.9</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse Online 7.9 changes Fuse Online 7.8 features as follows: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>New option for enabling the sample PostgresDB database and connection</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> By default, when you deploy Fuse Online, the sample PostgresDB database and connector are disabled (not installed). To enable them, edit the syndesis CR by setting the <code class="literal">demoData</code> option to <code class="literal">true</code>. For more information, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/installing_and_operating_fuse_online_on_openshift_container_platform/index#adding-sample-data_config">Adding sample data to a Fuse environment running on OCP</a> in <span class="emphasis"><em>Installing and Operating Fuse Online on OpenShift Container Platform</em></span>. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Slack connector now uses the Bot User OAuth Access Token</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> When you create a Slack connector, you now specify the Bot User OAuth Access Token to authorize access to your Slack app. Slack has deprecated the legacy token authorization. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Updates to the Fuse Online custom resource are applied when saved</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> When you make changes in the <code class="literal">components.server</code> section of the Fuse Online custom resource, Fuse Online applies your updates after you save the custom resource. Starting with Fuse Online 7.9, you no longer need to manually delete the <code class="literal">syndesis-server</code> pod for the changes to take effect. </p></li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="OnlineDistrib-UpgradeOnline">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.4.&nbsp;Upgrading Fuse Online integrations</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> To upgrade a Fuse Online environment that is running on OCP on-site, you must update Fuse Online by using the operator and then republish any running integrations as described in <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/installing_and_operating_fuse_online_on_openshift_container_platform/index#upgrade-on-ocp_manage">Upgrading Fuse Online</a>. </p>
         <p> Note that you should upgrade from Fuse Online 7.8 to 7.9 by using the OperatorHub, regardless of how you installed Fuse Online 7.8 (by using the install script or the OperatorHub). </p>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="OnlineDistrib-Important">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.5.&nbsp;Important notes for Fuse Online</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Important notes for the Fuse 7.9 release of the Fuse Online distribution: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>SOAP API Client connector features</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> The SOAP API client connector supports the following features: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="circle">
              <li class="listitem"> SOAP 1.1 and 1.2 message formats </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Both RPC and Document bindings only support Literal encoding. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> All Workday WSDLs use inline schemas, SOAP document literal binding, and WS Username Token text password authentication. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Nested circular reference types. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> External schemas - Only URL-based WSDLs support external schemas based on the relative URLs from the WSDL’s base path. The WSDL URL must be available to the SOAP connector at runtime for parsing and validation. Therefore, make sure that the WSDL and schemas are hosted at a permanent URL. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Multiple schemas - Both inline and external (WSDL URLs) support multiple schemas with unique namespaces. </li>
              <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> Security-related features: </p>
               <div class="itemizedlist">
                <ul class="itemizedlist" type="square">
                 <li class="listitem"> WS_Basic profile and list combinations. </li>
                 <li class="listitem"> For Basic Authentication, HTTPS username/password is supported. </li>
                 <li class="listitem"> For Username Token profiles, both Text and Digest passwords are supported. </li>
                </ul>
               </div></li>
             </ul>
            </div><p class="simpara"> In this release, the SOAP API client connector does not include support for the following features: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="circle">
              <li class="listitem"> External schemas - Disk-based external schemas referenced in WSDL files directly imported into the connector (by using the File Upload form) are not supported. Uploaded WSDL files must use inline schemas. However, URL-based WSDLs support external schemas hosted with the WSDLs. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> SOAP encoding is not supported. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> For security, SAML is not supported. </li>
             </ul>
            </div></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Kafka broker URIs not auto-discovered for AMQ Streams</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> The CRD version for AMQ Streams has increased in Fuse Online to <code class="literal">v1beta2</code> as described in <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_amq/2021.q2/html/release_notes_for_amq_streams_1.7_on_openshift/features-str#introducing_the_v1beta2_api_version">this AMQ release note</a>. If you are using AMQ Streams, when you create a new Kafka Message Broker connection in Fuse Online, the Kafka Broker URI is not auto-discovered and not shown in the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Kafka Broker URI</strong></span> drop-down list. Instead, you must type the URI. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"> Fuse Online no longer supports Camel K runtime or the KNative connector. </li>
           <li class="listitem"> When Fuse Online is installed and provisioned on Red Hat infrastructure, the account is limited to a specific number of integrations that can be running at one time. For details, see the pricing plan. </li>
           <li class="listitem"> An OpenAPI schema that you upload to Fuse Online might not define input/output types. When Fuse Online creates a custom API client from an OpenAPI schema that does not specify input/output types then it is not possible to create an integration that maps integration data to fields that the API client can process or from fields that the API client processed. If an integration requires data mapping to or from a custom API, then when you upload the OpenAPI schema, click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Review/Edit</strong></span> to open API Designer, which is an API editing tool, and add input/output type specifications. </li>
           <li class="listitem"> Since Fuse 7.8, an OpenAPI document that you use for a custom API client connector or for an API provider integration cannot have cyclic schema references. For example, a JSON schema that specifies a request or response body cannot reference itself as a whole nor reference any part of itself through any number of intermediate schemas. </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="OnlineDistrib-Support">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.6.&nbsp;Obtaining technical support for Fuse Online</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> To obtain technical support, in the Fuse Online console, in the left navigation panel, click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Support</strong></span>. Use the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Support</strong></span> page to download diagnostic information for all integrations or for one or more integrations that you choose. The page also provides a link for opening a support ticket and providing the diagnostic information that you downloaded. </p>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="OnlineDistrib-Technology-Preview">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">2.7.&nbsp;Technology Preview features in Fuse Online</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> This release includes the Technology Preview features that are listed below. </p>
         <div class="admonition important">
          <div class="admonition_header">
           Important
          </div>
          <div>
           <p> Technology Preview features are not supported with Red Hat production service level agreements (SLAs), might not be functionally complete, and Red Hat does not recommend using them in production. These features provide early access to upcoming product features, enabling customers to test functionality and provide feedback during the development process. For more information, see <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/support/offerings/techpreview/">Red Hat Technology Preview features support scope</a>. </p>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Fuse Online auditing</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> Fuse Online supports basic auditing for changes made by any user to the following Fuse Online components: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="circle">
              <li class="listitem"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Connections</strong></span> - The <code class="literal">Name</code> and any other fields shown on the connector’s <span class="strong strong"><strong>Details</strong></span> page in the Fuse Online web console. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Connectors</strong></span> - The <code class="literal">Name</code> field. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Integrations</strong></span> - The <code class="literal">Name</code> field. </li>
             </ul>
            </div></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/integrating_applications_with_fuse_online/index#applying-conditions-to-mappings_map">Conditional expressions for mapping data fields</a> </p><p class="simpara"> In the data mapper, you can specify a conditional expression and apply it to a data mapping. For example, a conditional expression can specify evaluation of a source field and how to populate the target field if the source field is empty. The limited set of expressions that you can specify are similar to Microsoft Excel expressions. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Document scope for user-defined properties in data mapper</strong></span> </p><p class="simpara"> In the data mapper, you can specify a scope for properties that you define for source and target mappings. In the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Mapping Details</strong></span> panel, click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Add</strong></span> (+) next to <span class="strong strong"><strong>Properties</strong></span>. In the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Create Property</strong></span> dialog. for the new <span class="strong strong"><strong>Scope</strong></span> option, you can select the current message header, a message header from a previous step, or <span class="strong strong"><strong>Camel Exchange Property</strong></span> for Camel-specific properties. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>For a REST API client that uses OAuth</strong></span>, when you create an API client connector, you can change the default OAuth2 behavior of connections that you create from that connector. Fuse Online vendor extensions to the OpenAPI specification support the following: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="circle">
              <li class="listitem"> Providing client credentials as parameters. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Obtaining a new access token based on HTTP response status codes. </li>
             </ul>
            </div></li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="FISDistrib">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;3.&nbsp;Fuse on OpenShift</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> Fuse on OpenShift enables you to deploy Fuse applications on OpenShift Container Platform. </p>
        <section class="section" id="FISDistrib-OpenShift">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">3.1.&nbsp;Supported version of OpenShift</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse on OpenShift is supported on OpenShift Container Platform 4.x and OpenShift Container Platform 3.11. For details of the supported version (or versions) of OpenShift Container Platform to use with Fuse on OpenShift, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/articles/310603">Supported Configurations</a> page. </p>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="FISDistrib-Containers">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">3.2.&nbsp;Supported images</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse on OpenShift provides the following Docker-formatted images: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-java-openshift-rhel8</code> — Spring Boot </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-java-openshift-jdk11-rhel8</code> — Spring Boot </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-karaf-openshift-rhel8</code> — Apache Karaf </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-eap-openshift-jdk8-rhel7</code> — Red Hat JBoss Enterprise Application Platform </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-eap-openshift-jdk11-rhel8</code> — Red Hat JBoss Enterprise Application Platform </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-console-rhel8</code> — Fuse console </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-console—​rhel8-operator</code> — Fuse console operator </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-apicurito-generator-rhel8</code> — Apicurito REST application generator </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-apicurito-rhel8</code> — Apicurito REST API editor </li>
           <li class="listitem"> <code class="literal">fuse7/fuse-apicurito-rhel8-operator</code> — API Designer Operator </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="FISDistrib-Features">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">3.3.&nbsp;New features in Fuse 7.9 on OpenShift</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse on OpenShift provides following new features in version 7.9: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> Support for JDK 11 </p><p class="simpara"> Fuse 7.9 offers support for building the Fuse on OpenShift quickstarts using JDK 11. </p></li>
           <li class="listitem"><p class="simpara"> Running quickstarts with <code class="literal">openshift-maven-plugin</code> </p><p class="simpara"> Fuse 7.9 uses new <code class="literal">openshift-maven-plugin</code> when building and running the Fuse on OpenShift quickstarts with Maven archtypes. </p></li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="FISDistrib-Important">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">3.4.&nbsp;Important notes</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Important notes for the Fuse 7.9 release of the Fuse on OpenShift distribution: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Data Virtualization has been removed</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Data Virtualization is deprecated since Fuse 7.7 and has been removed from Fuse 7.8. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Spring Boot 1 is has been removed</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Spring Boot 1 is deprecated since Fuse 7.7 and has been removed from Fuse 7.8. We recommend that you migrate your Spring Boot applications to Spring Boot 2, following the guidance in the <a class="link" href="https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-2.0-Migration-Guide">Spring Boot 2.0 Migration Guide</a>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fabric8 Maven plugin is now deprecated</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Fabric8 Maven plugin is deprecated and replaced with <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/fuse_on_openshift_guide/index#openshift-maven-plugin">OpenShift Maven plugin</a> since Fuse 7.9. Use OpenShift Maven plugin to build and deploy your applications. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Running quickstarts with JDK11</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Use the correct JDK11 profile during the compile time if you want to use JDK11 based image at runtime. When building and deploying the quickstarts using JDK11, ensure that you have installed JDK11 on your build machine and then build your quickstarts using the correct JDK11 profile. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">The <code class="literal">eap-camel-jpa</code> quickstart has been removed</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">eap-camel-jpa</code> quickstart has been removed from Fuse 7.8 due to an issue with a dependency. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Jolokia not externally accessible on Fuse 7.8</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Starting in Fuse 7.8, Jolokia default protocol is switched from HTTP to HTTPS. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="StandaloneDistrib">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;4.&nbsp;Fuse Standalone</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <section class="section" id="StandaloneDistrib-Containers">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">4.1.&nbsp;Supported containers</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse standalone 7.9 is supported on the following runtime containers: </p>
         <div class="itemizedlist">
          <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
           <li class="listitem"> Spring Boot 2 (standalone) </li>
           <li class="listitem"> Apache Karaf </li>
           <li class="listitem"> Red Hat JBoss Enterprise Application Platform (JBoss EAP) </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="StandaloneDistrib-Features">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">4.2.&nbsp;New features in Fuse 7.9</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The main new features of Fuse standalone in version 7.9 are: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Configuration of undertow thread pool names</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Undertow thread pools and their names can now be configured on a per-service/bundle basis to improve monitoring and debugging from the Hawtio console. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For more information, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_karaf_security_guide/index#worker_io_configuration">Worker IO configuration</a> section of the <span class="emphasis"><em>Apache Karaf Security Guide</em></span>. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Implement consumer priority in Camel</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Some brokers (and Artemis in particular) allow you to specify consumer priority for the messages you are sending. In Fuse 7.9 this configuration option is exposed in the <code class="literal">camel-amqp</code> and <code class="literal">camel-jms</code> components. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For more information, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_camel_component_reference/index#jms-component">JMS Component</a> section of the <span class="emphasis"><em>Apache Camel Component Reference</em></span>. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support for Salesforce Bulk API V2</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The Camel SAP Salesforce Bulk 2.0 API is now supported and can be used to quickly load a large amount of data into Salesforce, or query a large amount of data from Salesforce. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For more information, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_camel_component_reference/index#bulk_2_0_api">Bulk 2.0 API</a> section of the <span class="emphasis"><em>Apache Camel Component Reference</em></span>. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support for fast RFC serialization in the Camel SAP component</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The <code class="literal">camel-sap</code> component now supports fast RFC serialization. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For more information, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_camel_component_reference/index#SAP-DestConfig">Destination Configuration</a> section of the <span class="emphasis"><em>Apache Camel Component Reference</em></span>. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support Spring Security for Fuse on Karaf</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">camel-spring-security</code> component is now supported. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="StandaloneDistrib-TechPreview">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">4.3.&nbsp;Technology Preview features</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features of Fuse standalone are <span class="emphasis"><em>Technology Preview</em></span> only and are not supported in Fuse 7.9: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Saga EIP</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Saga Enterprise Integration Pattern (EIP) is a technology preview feature and features only the <span class="emphasis"><em>In-Memory</em></span> Saga service (which is not suitable for a production environments). The LRA Saga service is <span class="emphasis"><em>not</em></span> supported. For more details, see section <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/apache_camel_development_guide/index#saga-eip">Saga EIP</a> of the "Apache Camel Development Guide". 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
         <section class="section" id="fuse_tooling_support_for_apache_camel">
          <div class="titlepage">
           <div>
            <div>
             <h3 class="title">4.3.1.&nbsp;Fuse Tooling support for Apache Camel</h3>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <p> Fuse Tooling provides a cross-platform, cross-IDE approach to Camel application development, with Apache Camel language support extensions or plugins for Visual Studio Code, Eclipse IDE, and Eclipse Che. </p>
          <p> For Visual Studio Code, you can also add an extension that provides WSDL to Camel Rest DSL support. </p>
          <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Note:</strong></span> These features are already included by default with Fuse Tooling for Red Hat CodeReady Studio. </p>
          <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Visual Studio Code features</strong></span> </p>
          <div class="admonition note">
           <div class="admonition_header">
            Note
           </div>
           <div>
            <p> VS Code Apache Camel extensions are community features. They are not supported by Red Hat. </p>
           </div>
          </div>
          <p> The <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=camel-tooling.vscode-apache-camel">Language Support for Apache Camel</a> extension provides features for Camel URIs, such as the following: </p>
          <p> For XML DSL and Java DSL: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> You can navigate to endpoints in the VS Code <span class="strong strong"><strong>Outline</strong></span> panel and in the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Go &gt; Go to Symbol in File</strong></span> navigation panel. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you type, the editor provides code completion for Camel components, attributes, and the list of attribute values. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you hover over a Camel component, the editor shows a brief description of the component (from the <a class="link" href="http://camel.apache.org/components.html">Apache Camel component reference</a>). </li>
            <li class="listitem"> As you edit the file, the editor performs an Apache Camel validation check on the Camel code. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> You can specify a specific Camel Catalog version by selecting <span class="strong strong"><strong>File → Preferences → Settings → Apache Camel Tooling → Camel catalog version</strong></span>. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> You can use "Quick fix" features to address invalid enum values and unknown Camel URI component properties. </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> For XML DSL only: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> You can navigate to Camel contexts and routes in the VS Code <span class="strong strong"><strong>Outline</strong></span> panel and in the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Go &gt; Go to Symbol in File</strong></span> navigation panel. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you type, the editor provides code completion for referenced IDs of <code class="literal">direct</code>, <code class="literal">direct VM</code>, <code class="literal">VM</code> and <code class="literal">SEDA</code> components. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> You can find references for <code class="literal">direct</code> and <code class="literal">direct VM</code> components in all open Camel files. </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> For Properties: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> Completion for Camel component property </li>
            <li class="listitem"> Diagnostic </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> The <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=camel-tooling.vscode-wsdl2rest">WSDL 2 Camel Rest DSL</a> extension (<a class="link" href="https://github.com/camel-tooling/vscode-wsdl2rest">wsdl2rest</a> implementation) provides WSDL to Camel Rest DSL support. By specifying an existing WSDL file, you can use this extension to generate a Camel Rest DSL + CXF solution for REST-style access. The WSDL file can be located either on your local file system or from an accessible web URL. </p>
          <p> To access the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Language Support for Apache Camel</strong></span> and <span class="strong strong"><strong>WSDL to Camel Rest DSL</strong></span> features, you add one or more extensions. </p>
          <p> The <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=camel-tooling.apache-camel-extension-pack">Apache Camel Extension Pack</a> installs the following VS Code extensions: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=camel-tooling.vscode-apache-camel">Language Support for Apache Camel</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.vscode-openshift-connector">OpenShift Connector</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=vscjava.vscode-java-pack">Java Extension Pack</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=Pivotal.vscode-boot-dev-pack">Spring Boot extension pack</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.project-initializer">Project initializer by Red Hat</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=camel-tooling.vscode-wsdl2rest">WSDL 2 Camel Rest DSL</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.vscode-xml">XML Language Support</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.atlasmap-viewer">AtlasMap Data Transformation editor</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.vscode-didact">Didact Tutorial</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> <a class="link" href="https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=redhat.vscode-camelk">Tooling for Apache Camel K</a> </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> Optionally, you can install the extensions individually. </p>
          <p> For more details, see the following readme files: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> Readme for <a class="link" href="https://github.com/camel-tooling/vscode-camel-extension-pack">Apache Camel Extension Pack</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> Readme for <a class="link" href="https://github.com/camel-tooling/camel-lsp-client-vscode">Apache Camel Language Server Protocol for Visual Studio Code</a> </li>
            <li class="listitem"> Readme for <a class="link" href="https://github.com/camel-tooling/vscode-wsdl2rest">WSDL to Camel Rest DSL</a> </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Eclipse IDE features</strong></span> </p>
          <p> The <span class="strong strong"><strong>Language Support for Apache Camel</strong></span> Eclipse plug-in provides the following features for Camel URIs: </p>
          <p> In the generic Eclipse text editor for both XML DSL and Java DSL: </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> When you type, the editor provides code completion for Camel components, attributes, and the list of attribute values. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you hover over a Camel component, the editor shows a brief description of the component (from the <a class="link" href="http://camel.apache.org/components.html">Apache Camel component reference</a>). </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> When you use the Eclipse XML or Java editor, only the auto-completion feature is provided. </p>
          <p> To access the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Language Support for Apache Camel</strong></span> features, you install the Eclipse plug-in from the Eclipse Marketplace. For more details, see the <a class="link" href="https://github.com/camel-tooling/camel-lsp-client-eclipse">readme file</a> for Apache Camel Language Server Protocol for Eclipse IDE. </p>
          <p> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Eclipse Che features</strong></span> </p>
          <p> The <span class="strong strong"><strong>Language Support for Apache Camel</strong></span> plugin for Eclipse Che 7 provides features for Camel URIs in XML DSL and Java DSL. </p>
          <div class="itemizedlist">
           <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
            <li class="listitem"> When you type, the editor provides code completion for Camel components, attributes, and the list of attribute values. </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you hover over a Camel component, the editor shows a brief description of the component (from the <a class="link" href="http://camel.apache.org/components.html">Apache Camel component reference</a>). </li>
            <li class="listitem"> When you save the file, the editor performs an Apache Camel validation check on the Camel code. </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
          <p> To activate this plugin for Eclipse Che, you can use the "Apache Camel based on Spring Boot" stack or edit your workspace configuration. </p>
         </section>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="StandaloneDistrib-BOMs">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">4.4.&nbsp;BOM files for Fuse 7.9</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> To configure your Maven projects to use the supported Fuse 7.9 artifacts, use the BOM versions documented in this section. </p>

          <p> For more details about using the BOM, see the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/migration_guide/index">Migration Guide</a>. </p>
