        <section class="section" id="StandaloneDistrib-Important">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">4.5.&nbsp;Important notes</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Important notes for the Fuse 7.9 release of the Fuse standalone distribution: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse on EAP is upgraded to use JBoss EAP 7.4.0 (from JBoss EAP 7.3.2)</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Fuse 7.9 release now runs on the JBoss Enterprise Application Platform (EAP) 7.4 container (upgraded from JBoss EAP 7.3.2 in the previous release of Fuse). For more details, see JBoss EAP 7.4.0 Release Notes. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Updated Jackson libraries</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Updated the Jackson libraries from 2.9 and 2.10 to 2.12.1. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Using OpenJDK 8u292 with Apache Karaf</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             When running Fuse in Apache Karaf, Red Hat recommend using OpenJDK 8u282. Do not use OpenJDK 8u292 which has a known issue affecting the credential store. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Upgrading Fuse on Karaf</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The Fuse 7.9 release restores the Apache Karaf mechanism (removed in Fuse 7.8) which enables you to apply fixes to an Apache Karaf container without needing to reinstall an updated version of Fuse on Karaf. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For more details on upgrading to Fuse 7.9 on Karaf, see <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/migration_guide/index#upgrading-fuse-standalone-on-karaf">Fuse Migration Guide</a>. </p>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="deprecatedandremoved">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;5.&nbsp;Deprecated and Removed Features</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> If you need any assistance or have any questions about the upcoming changes in Fuse 7, contact <a class="link" href="mailto:support@redhat.com">support@redhat.com</a>. </p>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-deprecated">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.1.&nbsp;Deprecated</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features are deprecated in Fuse 7.9 and may be removed in a future release: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">fabric8-maven-plugin is deprecated</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.9, the <code class="literal">fabric8-maven-plugin</code> is deprecated. From Fuse 7.9 onward, we recommend that you use the <code class="literal">openshift-maven-plugin</code> instead for building and deploying Maven projects in Fuse on OpenShift. The plugin is maintained by Eclipse JKube, which provides extensive <a class="link" href="https://www.eclipse.org/jkube/docs/openshift-maven-plugin">documentation</a> for the plugin. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse Online install script for installation on OCP 4</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.8, the Fuse Online install script is deprecated for installing Fuse Online on OpenShift Container Platform (OCP) 4.x versions. On OCP 4.x versions, we recommend that you use the Fuse Online Operator. The Fuse Online install script is still supported for installing Fuse Online on OCP 3.11. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">PHP, Python, and Ruby scripting languages are deprecated in Camel applications</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The PHP, Python, and Ruby scripting languages are deprecated in Camel applications since Fuse 7.4 and will be removed in a future release. The Camel community has deprecated PHP, Python, and Ruby since Camel 2.19 (see <a class="link" href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CAMEL-10973">CAMEL-10973</a>). This applies to all Fuse containers types: Apache Karaf, JBoss EAP, and Spring Boot. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">HP-UX OS is deprecated</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The HP-UX operating system is deprecated since Fuse 7.2 and support for this operating system could be removed in a future release of Fuse. In particular, note that the JBoss EAP 7.2 container has already dropped support for HP-UX and, consequently, any future version of Fuse on JBoss EAP that runs on JBoss EAP 7.2 will <span class="emphasis"><em>not</em></span> be supported on HP-UX. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel MQTT component is deprecated</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel MQTT component is deprecated in Fuse 7.0 and will be removed in a future release of Fuse. You can use the Camel Paho component instead, which supports the MQTT messaging protocol using the popular <a class="link" href="https://eclipse.org/paho/">Eclipse Paho</a> library. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel LevelDB component is deprecated on all operating systems except for Linux</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 6.3, the Camel LevelDB (<code class="literal">camel-leveldb</code>) component is deprecated on all operating systems except for Red Hat Enterprise Linux. In future, the Camel LevelDB component will be supported only on Red Hat Enterprise Linux. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">BatchMessage class from the Camel SJMS component is deprecated</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The BatchMessage class from the Camel SJMS component is deprecated in Fuse 7 (deprecated in Apache Camel since version 2.17) and may be removed from a future version of Apache Camel and Fuse. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-removed-78">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.2.&nbsp;Removed in Fuse 7.8</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Spring Boot 1</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Spring Boot 1 is no longer supported in Fuse 7.8. We recommend that you migrate your Spring Boot applications to Spring Boot 2, following the guidance in the <a class="link" href="https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-2.0-Migration-Guide">Spring Boot 2.0 Migration Guide</a>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel K runtime in Fuse Online</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Camel K runtime in Fuse Online (technology preview feature) is no longer supported in Fuse 7.8. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel XmlJson component has been removed in 7.8</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel XmlJson (<code class="literal">camel-xmljson</code>) component has been removed in Fuse 7.8. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-removed-75">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.3.&nbsp;Removed in Fuse 7.5</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features were removed in Fuse 7.5: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support for integration with MS SQL Server 2014 has been dropped in 7.5</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             MS SQL Server 2014 is no longer tested and supported for integrations with Fuse 7.5. We recommend that you use one of the more recent versions of MS SQL Server instead — for example, MS SQL Server 2016 or 2017. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel LinkedIn component has been removed in 7.5</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The <code class="literal">camel-linkedin</code> component has been removed in Fuse 7.5. </p>
            <div class="admonition important">
             <div class="admonition_header">
              Important
             </div>
             <div>
              <p> Although removed from Fuse 7.5, the <code class="literal">camel-linkedin</code> component is likely to be restored in a later release. </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-removed-73">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.4.&nbsp;Removed in Fuse 7.3</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features were removed in Fuse 7.3: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel YQL component has been removed in 7.3</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel YQL component has been removed in Fuse 7.3. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">OpenJPA and OpenJPA3 Karaf features have been removed in 7.3</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">openjpa</code> feature and the <code class="literal">openjpa3</code> feature have been removed from the Apache Karaf container in 7.3. For a Java Persistence Architecture (JPA) implementation, use the supported <code class="literal">hibernate</code> feature instead. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">camel-jetty Karaf feature has been removed in 7.3</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">camel-jetty</code> feature has been removed from the Apache Karaf container in 7.3, because it uses Jetty 8. Use the <code class="literal">camel-jetty9</code> feature instead. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">pax-jms-oracleaq Karaf feature has been removed in 7.3</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">pax-jms-oracleaq</code> feature has been removed from the Apache Karaf container in 7.3, because it requires 3rd party, non-free Oracle AQ libraries. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">camel-elasticsearch component has been removed from Fuse on EAP (Wildfly Camel) in 7.3</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">camel-elasticsearch</code> component has been removed from Fuse on EAP (Wildfly Camel) in 7.3. Use the newer <code class="literal">camel-elasticsearch-rest</code> component instead. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-removed-72">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.5.&nbsp;Removed in Fuse 7.2</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features were removed in Fuse 7.2: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel XMLRPC component has been removed in 7.2</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel XMLRPC component has been removed in Fuse 7.2. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel Netty component has been removed in 7.2</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel Netty component has been removed in Fuse 7.2. It is recommended that you use the Camel Netty4 component instead. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-removed-70">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.6.&nbsp;Removed in Fuse 7.0</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features were removed in Fuse 7.0: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support for Red Hat JBoss Operations Network (JON) has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, Fuse on Karaf no longer supports JON and no longer provides JON plugins for integrating with the JON runtime. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Embedded ActiveMQ broker has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, Fuse on Karaf no longer provides an embedded ActiveMQ Broker. Customers should connect to a supported remote broker directly. For more information on our supported brokers, refer to the "Supported Messaging Providers" section of the <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/articles/310603">Red Hat Fuse Supported Configurations page</a>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Fuse integration pack has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Support for running rules and processes is provided by components shipped with Red Hat JBoss BPM Suite and Red Hat JBoss BRMS. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Karaf console commands for child container administration have been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Since Fuse 7.0, the Karaf console commands for child container administration are <span class="emphasis"><em>not</em></span> supported. That is, the console commands prefixed by <code class="literal">instance:</code> (Karaf 4.x syntax) and the console commands prefixed by <code class="literal">admin:</code> (Karaf 2.x syntax) are not supported. </p>
            <div class="admonition note">
             <div class="admonition_header">
              Note
             </div>
             <div>
              <p> In the Fuse 7.0 GA release, the <code class="literal">instance:</code> commands are not removed. This is a known issue. </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">SwitchYard has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, SwitchYard has been removed, and you should use Apache Camel directly instead. For more detailed information, see the knowledge base article, <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/solutions/3063561">SwitchYard Support Plan After Releasing Fuse 7</a>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Support for Fabric8 1.x has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Since Fuse 7.0, Fabric8 v1 has been replaced by Fuse on OpenShift (previously, Fuse Integration Services), which includes components of Fabric8 v2 technology. Fuse on OpenShift provides a set of tools and Docker-formatted images that enable development, deployment, and management of integration microservices within OpenShift. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> Although Fuse on OpenShift has a different architecture, it fulfills the same provisioning, automation, central configuration and management requirements that Fabric8 v1 provides. For more information, see <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.9/html-single/fuse_on_openshift_guide/index">Fuse on OpenShift Guide</a>. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel components for Google App Engine have been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel components for Google App Engine (<code class="literal">camel-gae</code>) have been removed in Fuse 7.0. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Camel jBPM component has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Camel jBPM component (<code class="literal">camel-jbpm</code>) has been removed in Fuse 7.0. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Tanuki based wrapper for installing Fuse as a service has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Tanuki based wrapper scripts — generated using the <code class="literal">wrapper:install</code> Karaf console command — for installing Fuse as a service have been removed in Fuse 7.0. To install the Apache Karaf container as a service, it is recommended that you use the new <code class="literal">karaf-service-*.sh</code> scripts from the <code class="literal">bin/contrib</code> directory instead. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Smooks has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, the Smooks component for SwitchYard has been removed. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">BPEL has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             BPEL (based on the <a class="link" href="http://riftsaw.jboss.org/">Riftsaw</a> project) has been removed from Fuse 7.0. If you are currently using BPEL, it is recommended that you consider migrating to the Red Hat JBoss BPM Suite. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Design Time Governance has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Design Time Governance component has been removed in 7.0. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Runtime Governance has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, the Runtime Governance (RTGov) component has been removed. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">S-RAMP has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The SOA Repository Artifact Model and Protocol (S-RAMP) component has been removed in Fuse 7.0. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">bin/patch script has been removed in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <code class="literal">bin/patch</code> script (<code class="literal">bin\patch.bat</code> on Windows O/S) has been removed in a Fuse 7.0. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Spring Dynamic Modules (Spring-DM) is not supported in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Spring-DM (which integrates Spring XML with the OSGi service layer in Apache Karaf) is not supported in Fuse 7.0 and you should use the Blueprint framework instead. Using Blueprint XML does not prevent you from using the Java libraries from the Spring framework: the latest version of Spring is compatible with Blueprint. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Apache OpenJPA is not supported in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The <a class="link" href="https://openjpa.apache.org/">Apache OpenJPA</a> implementation of the Java Persistence API (JPA) is not supported in Fuse7.0. It is recommended that you use the <a class="link" href="http://hibernate.org/orm/">Hibernate</a> implementation instead. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="deprecatedandremoved-replaced-70">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">5.7.&nbsp;Replaced in Fuse 7.0</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The following features were replaced in Fuse 7.0: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Geronimo transaction manager has been replaced in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.0, the Geronimo transaction manager in the Karaf container has been replaced by <a class="link" href="http://narayana.io/">Narayana</a>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">Jetty container has been replaced in 7.0</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.0, the Jetty container has been replaced by <a class="link" href="http://undertow.io/">Undertow</a>. Initially, this change applies only to internal use of the Jetty container (for example, in the Karaf container). Other Jetty components might be removed in a future release. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="Unsupported">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;6.&nbsp;Unsupported Features in Fuse 7.9</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> The following features are unsupported in Red Hat Fuse 7.9. </p>
        <div class="variablelist">
         <dl class="variablelist">
          <dt>
           <span class="term">Installation of Fuse Console using the Operator is not supported on OCP 3.11</span>
          </dt>
          <dd>
            Installation of the Fuse Console using the Operator is not supported and does not work on OpenShift Container Platform (OCP) 3.11. The recommended way to install Fuse Console on OCP 3.11 is to use templates. 
          </dd>
          <dt>
           <span class="term">Apache Karaf EclipseLink feature is unsupported</span>
          </dt>
          <dd>
            The Apache Karaf EclipseLink feature is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Fuse, because this feature depends on JPA 2.2, while the Karaf container for Fuse 7.2 is aligned with JPA 2.1. 
          </dd>
          <dt>
           <span class="term">Apache Aries Blueprint Web module is unsupported</span>
          </dt>
          <dd>
            The Apache Aries <a class="link" href="http://aries.apache.org/modules/blueprintweb.html">Blueprint Web</a> module is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Fuse. The presence of an example featuring Blueprint Web in the community edition of Apache Camel (provided as a separate download) does <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> imply that this feature is supported in Fuse. 
          </dd>
          <dt>
           <span class="term">The PHP scripting language is not supported in Apache Camel on Apache Karaf</span>
          </dt>
          <dd>
            The PHP scripting language is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Camel applications on the Apache Karaf container, because there is no OSGi bundle available for PHP. The PHP scripting language is deprecated in Camel applications on the JBoss EAP container and on the Spring Boot container. 
          </dd>
          <dt>
           <span class="term">The Python scripting language is not supported in Apache Camel on Apache Karaf</span>
          </dt>
          <dd>
            The Python scripting language is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Camel applications on the Apache Karaf container, because there is no OSGi bundle available for Python. The Python scripting language is deprecated in Camel applications on the JBoss EAP container and on the Spring Boot container. 
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </div>
       </section>
       <section class="chapter" id="known-issues">
        <div class="titlepage">
         <div>
          <div>
           <h1 class="title">Chapter&nbsp;7.&nbsp;Known Issues</h1>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p> The following subsections describe the known issues in version 7.9. </p>
        <section class="section" id="cve-security-vulnerabilities">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.1.&nbsp;CVE Security Vulnerabilities</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> As a middleware integration platform, Fuse can potentially be integrated with a large number of third-party components. It is not always possible to exclude the possibility that some third-party dependencies of Fuse could have security vulnerabilities. This section documents known common vulnerabilities and exposures (CVEs) related to security that affect third-party dependencies of Fuse 7.9. </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/security/cve/cve-2020-13936">CVE-2020-13936</a></em></span> CVE-2020-13936 velocity: arbitrary code execution when attacker is able to modify templates</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> An attacker that is able to modify Velocity templates may execute arbitrary Java code or run arbitrary system commands with the same privileges as the account running the Servlet container. This applies to applications that allow untrusted users to upload/modify velocity templates running Apache Velocity Engine versions up to 2.2. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> Fuse 7.9 has modified its dependencies to ensure that it uses only the Velocity version (that is, version 2.3) that has been fixed to protect against this security vulnerability. If your application code has any explicit dependencies on the Apache Velocity component, we recommend that you upgrade these dependencies to use the fixed version. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-8113">ENTESB-8113</a></em></span> CVE-2018-10237 guava: Unbounded memory allocation in AtomicDoubleArray and CompoundOrdering classes allow remote attackers to cause a denial of service [fuse-7.0.0]</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Google Guava versions 11.0 through 24.1 are vulnerable to unbounded memory allocation in the <code class="literal">AtomicDoubleArray</code> class (when serialized with Java serialization) and the <code class="literal">CompoundOrdering</code> class (when serialized with GWT serialization). An attacker could exploit applications that use Guava and deserialize untrusted data to cause a denial of service — for more details, see <a class="link" href="https://github.com/google/guava/wiki/CVE-2018-10237">CVE-2018-10237</a>. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> To avoid this security vulnerability, we recommend that you: </p>
            <div class="itemizedlist">
             <ul class="itemizedlist" type="disc">
              <li class="listitem"> Never deserialize an <code class="literal">AtomicDoubleArray</code> instance or a <code class="literal">CompoundOrdering</code> instance from an unknown source. </li>
              <li class="listitem"> Avoid using Guava versions 24 and earlier (although in some cases it is not possible to avoid the earlier versions). </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
            <p class="simpara"> To make it easier to avoid the earlier (vulnerable) versions of Guava, Fuse 7.7 has configured its Maven Bill of Materials (BOM) files for all containers to select Guava 27 by default. This means that if you incorporate a Fuse BOM into your Maven project (by adding a dependency on the BOM to the <code class="literal">dependencyManagement</code> section of your POM file) and then specify a dependency on the Guava artifact <span class="emphasis"><em>without</em></span> specifying an explicit version, the Guava version will default to the version specified in the BOM, which is version 27 for the Fuse 7.7 BOMs. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> But there is at least one common use case involving the Apache Karaf (OSGi) container, where it is not possible to avoid using a vulnerable version of Guava: if your OSGi application uses Guava and Swagger together, you are obliged to use Guava 20, because that is the version required by Swagger. Here we explain why this is the case and how to configure your POM file to revert the earlier (vulnerable) Guava 20 library. First, you need to understand the concept of a <span class="emphasis"><em>double OSGi chain</em></span>. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Double OSGi chain</strong></span> </p>
            <p class="simpara"> Bundles in the OSGi runtime are <span class="emphasis"><em>wired</em></span> together using package constraints (package name + optional version/range) — imports and exports. Each bundle can have multiple imports and usually those imports wire a given bundle with multiple bundles. For example: </p>
            <pre class="screen">BundleA
+-- BundleB
|   +-- BundleCa
+-- BundleCb</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> Where <code class="literal">BundleA</code> depends on <code class="literal">BundleB</code> and <code class="literal">BundleCb</code>, while <code class="literal">BundleB</code> depends on <code class="literal">BundleCa</code>. <code class="literal">BundleCa</code> and <code class="literal">BundleCb</code> should be the same bundle, if the export the same packages, but due to version (range) constraints, <code class="literal">BundleB</code> uses (<span class="emphasis"><em>wires to</em></span>) a different revision/version of <code class="literal">BundleC</code> than <code class="literal">BundleA</code>. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> Rewriting the preceding diagram to reflect what happens when you include dependencies on both Guava and Swagger in an application: </p>
            <pre class="screen">org.jboss.qe.cxf.rs.swagger-deployment
+-- Guava 27
+-- Swagger 1.5
    +-- reflections 0.9.11
        +-- Guava 20</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> If you try to deploy this bundle configuration, you get the error, <code class="literal">org.osgi.framework.BundleException: Uses constraint violation</code>. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> <span class="strong strong"><strong>Reverting to Guava 20</strong></span> </p>
            <p class="simpara"> If your project uses both Guava and Swagger libraries (directly or indirectly), you should configure the <code class="literal">maven-bundle-plugin</code> to use an explicit version range (or no range at all) for the Guava bundle import, as follows: </p>
            <pre class="programlisting language-xml">&lt;Import-Package&gt;
    com.google.common.base;version="[20.0,21.0)",
    com.google.common.collect;version="[20.0,21.0)",
    com.google.common.io;version="[20.0,21.0)"
&lt;/Import-Package&gt;</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> This configuration forces your OSGi application to revert to the (vulnerable) Guava 20 library. It is therefore particularly important to avoid deserializing <code class="literal">AtomicDoubleArray</code> instances in this case. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/security/vulnerabilities/CVE-2017-12629">CVE-2017-12629</a></em></span> Solr/Lucene -security bypass to access sensitive data - CVE-2017-12629</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Apache Solr is a popular open source search platform that uses the Apache Lucene search engine. If your application uses a combination of Apache Solr with Apache Lucene (for example, when using the Camel Solr component), it could be affected by this security vulnerability. Please consult the linked security advisory for more details of this vulnerability and the mitigation steps to take. </p>
            <div class="admonition note">
             <div class="admonition_header">
              Note
             </div>
             <div>
              <p> The Fuse runtime does <span class="emphasis"><em>not</em></span> use Apache Solr or Apache Lucene directly. The security risk only arises, if you are using Apache Solr and Apache Lucene together in the context of an integration application (for example, when using the Camel Solr component). </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-fuse-online">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.2.&nbsp;Fuse Online</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> The Fuse Online distribution has the following known issues: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-17137">ENTESB-17137</a></em></span> Cannot access Fuse Online on disconnected environment</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> In Fuse 7.9, after installing Fuse Online on a disconnected OpenShift Container Platform (OCP) cluster, you cannot access the UI for Fuse Online. When you try to access the UI, you get the following error: </p>
            <pre class="screen">504 Gateway Time-out
The server didn't respond in time.</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> To work around this issue, you need to scale the Fuse Online Operator down to zero, and then set three environment variables in the Syndesis OAuth Proxy deployment configuration. You can do this at the command line, by entering the following commands: </p>
            <pre class="screen">oc scale deployment fuse-online-operator --replicas 0
sleep 10
oc set env deploymentconfig/syndesis-oauthproxy HTTP_PROXY=$(oc get proxy cluster -o jsonpath='{.status.httpProxy}')
oc set env deploymentconfig/syndesis-oauthproxy HTTPS_PROXY=$(oc get proxy cluster -o jsonpath='{.status.httpsProxy}')
oc set env deploymentconfig/syndesis-oauthproxy NO_PROXY=$(oc get proxy cluster -o jsonpath='{.status.noProxy}')</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> Note that the Fuse Online Operator <span class="strong strong"><strong>must remain scaled at zero</strong></span>. If you scale the Operator back to one, it will overwrite the environment variables, resetting them to the (incorrect) default values. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16987">ENTESB-16987</a></em></span> [Hawtio] Broken layout for drop-down menu in OSGi → Features</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.8, when using the Fuse Console on Apache Karaf, on the <span class="strong strong"><strong>OSGi | Features</strong></span> tab, the <span class="strong strong"><strong>Filter by repository</strong></span> dropdown menu has a bad layout. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16989">ENTESB-16989</a></em></span> DataMapper backslash delimiter in split transformation works only when the message has double backslashes</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.9, when using the DataMapper <code class="literal">one-to-many</code> split transformation, if you choose the backslash character, <code class="literal">\</code>, as the delimiter to define the split points, the split transformation will succeed only if the backslash character is escaped by another backslash. In other words, the splits are made on each occurrence of a double backslash, <code class="literal">\\</code>. The JSON standard requires backslash literals to be escaped by another backslash, so this behavior is consistent with the JSON standard. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16990">ENTESB-16990</a></em></span> DataMapper multi spaces delimiter in split transformation behaves as "double spaces" delimiter</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.9, when using the DataMapper <code class="literal">one-to-many</code> split transformation, if you choose a multi-space delimiter consisting of more than two spaces to define the split points, the split content will contain additional space(s). For example, when using a multi-space delimiter consisting of <code class="literal">n</code> spaces, the resulting split fields will be preceeded by <code class="literal">n-2</code> spaces. In other words, the split transformation behaves as if it was splitting on a double space. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-15063">ENTESB-15063</a></em></span> Unable to override maven repositories</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Since Fuse 7.8, if you are running Fuse Online in an offline (disconnected from the internet) environment and you have configured the Fuse Online custom resource (CR) to use a custom Maven repository on your local network, for example: </p>
            <pre class="screen">...
      server:
        features:
          maven:
            append: false
            repositories:
              customRepo1: http://192.0.2.0:8080
...</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> Then there are particular circumstances where other Maven repositories are consulted, in addition to the specified <code class="literal">customRepo1</code>, in spite of the fact that the <code class="literal">append: false</code> flag is specified in the CR. For example, this can happen if Fuse Online is configured to use extensions that download Maven dependencies while they are building. Typically, this issue causes longer build times, because the incorrect Maven repositories are consulted <span class="strong strong"><strong>before</strong></span> the specified custom Maven repository, which wastes time during the build process. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-15348">ENTESB-15348</a></em></span> Syndesis-jaeger uses unproductized image on OCP 3.11</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Since Fuse 7.8, if you are attempting to install Fuse Online on OCP 3.11 with the Jaeger add-on enabled (enhanced activity tracking), it is possible you might encounter the following error: </p>
            <pre class="screen">Unknown desc = toomanyrequests: You have reached your pull rate limit. You may increase the limit by authenticating and upgrading: https://www.docker.com/increase-rate-limit</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> This happens because the productised Jaeger container references Dockerhub images, which are out of Red Hat’s control. To work around this issue, you can either wait until rate limit window times out, or disable the Jaeger add-on. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-14518">ENTESB-14518</a></em></span> Jaeger operator installed by Syndesis 1.11 affects other namespaces</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.8, when you install Fuse 7.8 Online (Syndesis 1.11) on an OpenShift cluster, the Jaeger Operator (which gets installed along with Fuse Online) is configured to manage <span class="emphasis"><em>All namespaces</em></span> by default. A side effect of this behavior is that, in the case where you already have Fuse 7.7 Online (Syndesis 1.10) installed on a cluster and then you install Fuse 7.8 Online in a different namespace, the Jaeger Operator installed with Fuse 7.8 Online tries to manage the (older) Jaeger instance installed on the Fuse 7.7 Online namespace. The result is that a new <code class="literal">syndesis-jaeger</code> pod — in addition to the existing <code class="literal">syndesis-jaeger</code> pod — appears in the Fuse 7.7 Online namespace and the new <code class="literal">syndesis-jaeger</code> pod enters the <code class="literal">CrashLoopBackOff</code> state. The original Fuse 7.7 Online instance is not affected and the crashed <code class="literal">syndesis-jaeger</code> pod can be safely ignored. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-13966">ENTESB-13966</a></em></span> Discovery of deployed integration API seems disabled but not really</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Starting in Fuse 7.7, after creating a new integration containing an API, the integration detail page wrongly implies that 3scale discovery is disabled for this integration. Additionally, the integration detail page does not show the API URL. By clicking this button three times (click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Enable</strong></span>, then click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Disable</strong></span>, then click <span class="strong strong"><strong>Enable</strong></span>), you can resynchronize the page so that 3scale discovery is enabled and the API URL is displayed. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-fuse-openshift">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.3.&nbsp;Fuse on OpenShift</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> This section lists issues that affect the deployment of Fuse applications on OpenShift. For details of issues affecting specific containers, see also the sections for Spring Boot, Fuse on Apache Karaf, and Fuse on JBoss EAP. The Fuse on OpenShift distribution has the following known issues: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-17144">ENTESB-17144</a></em></span> Fuse Camel project generated by Apicurito Generator not exposes management port</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> In Fuse 7.9, a Fuse Camel project generated by API Designer (Apicurito Generator) does not expose a management port, because the file, <code class="literal">src/main/resources/application.yml</code> is configured incorrectly. The generated <code class="literal">src/main/resources/application.yml</code> file has the following configuration: </p>
            <pre class="screen">management:
  port: 8081
endpoints:
  enabled: false
  health:
    enabled: true</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> This configuration must be changed to: </p>
            <pre class="screen">management:
  server:
    port: 8081

  endpoints:
    enabled-by-default: false

  endpoint:
    health:
      enabled: true</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> Moreover, the <code class="literal">pom.xml</code> file in the generated project uses the <code class="literal">fabric8-maven-plugin</code>, which is deprecated. It is preferable to use the new <code class="literal">openshift-maven-plugin</code> in a Maven project. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-17125">ENTESB-17125</a></em></span> Quickstart Spring-Boot Soap2Rest integration tests fail because of invalid algorithm parameter</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.9, the Spring Boot Soap2Rest integration tests are failing, but this does not affect the functionality. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-17091">ENTESB-17091</a></em></span> Missing metering labels on spring-boot-camel-rhosak quickstart</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.9, Fuse running on Spring Boot 2 does not support metering labels. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-15994">ENTESB-15994</a></em></span> API Designer upgrade from 7.8 to 7.9 requires delete and reinstall</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.9, The normal operator upgrade process does not work when upgrading from API Designer 7.8 to API Designer 7.9. To upgrade the API Designer from Fuse 7.8 to Fuse 7.9, you must delete the 7.8 API Designer operator and then install the 7.9 API Designer operator. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16814">ENTESB-16814</a></em></span> Monitoring resources are linked wrongly from the documentation</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.8, the locations of the monitoring resources referenced in section <a class="link" href="https://access.redhat.com/documentation/en-us/red_hat_fuse/7.8/html-single/fuse_on_openshift_guide/index#prometheus-set-up">2.5.2. Setting up Prometheus</a> of the <span class="emphasis"><em>Fuse on OpenShift Guide</em></span> are incorrect and return a 404 exception. This documented procedure will be fixed in a post-GA documentation update. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16287">ENTESB-16287</a></em></span> Unable to start Karaf</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> In Fuse 7.9, when building a Karaf application to run on OpenShift, you must edit the <code class="literal">pom.xml</code>, adding a line to the <code class="literal">Import-Package</code> section of the POM file to specify the explicit version range for <code class="literal">javax.annotation;version="[1.3,2.0)"</code> for the <code class="literal">javax.annotation</code> package. </p>
            <p class="simpara"> For example, if the <code class="literal">Import-Package</code> section in your <code class="literal">pom.xml</code> file looks like this: </p>
            <pre class="screen">&lt;Import-Package&gt;
   javax.ws.rs;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.ws.rs.core;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.ws.rs.ext;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.xml.bind;version="[2,3)",
   javax.xml.bind.annotation;version="[2,3)",
   org.osgi.service.blueprint,
   org.apache.cxf.transport.http,
   *
&lt;/Import-Package&gt;</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> You would add a line with <code class="literal">javax.annotation;version="[1.3,2.0)"</code>, so that the section looks like: </p>
            <pre class="screen">&lt;Import-Package&gt;
   javax.annotation;version="[1.3,2.0)",
   javax.ws.rs;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.ws.rs.core;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.ws.rs.ext;version="[2, 3)",
   javax.xml.bind;version="[2,3)",
   javax.xml.bind.annotation;version="[2,3)",
   org.osgi.service.blueprint,
   org.apache.cxf.transport.http,
   *
&lt;/Import-Package&gt;</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> The reason this is needed is because some common third-party dependencies can pull in the wrong version of the <code class="literal">javax.annotations</code> library into the Karaf container. </p>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-fuse-karaf">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.4.&nbsp;Fuse on Apache Karaf</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse on Apache Karaf has the following known issues: </p>
         <div class="variablelist" id="known-issue-entesb-16417">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16417">ENTESB-16417</a></em></span> Credential store is using PBEWithSHA1AndDESede by default</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The security API in OpenJDK 8u292 and in OracleJDK 1.8.0_291 returns an incomplete list of security providers, which causes the credential store in Apache Karaf to fail (because the required security provider appears to be unavailable). The underlying issue that causes this problem is <a class="link" href="https://bugs.openjdk.java.net/browse/JDK-8249906">https://bugs.openjdk.java.net/browse/JDK-8249906</a>. We recommend that you use the earlier OpenJDK version, OpenJDK 8u282, or the later OpenJDK version, OpenJDK 8u302, which do not have this bug. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16526">ENTESB-16526</a></em></span> fuse-karaf on Windows cannot restart during patch:install</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> While running <code class="literal">patch:install</code> in the Apache Karaf container on the Windows platform, under certain circumstances you might encounter the following error when the <code class="literal">patch:install</code> command attempts an automatic restart of the container: </p>
            <pre class="screen">Red Hat Fuse starting up. Press Enter to open the shell now...
100% [========================================================================]
Karaf started in 18s. Bundle stats: 235 active, 235 total
'.tmpdir' is not recognized as an internal or external command,
operable program or batch file.
There is a Root instance already running with name ~14 and pid ~13. If you know what you are doing and want to force the run anyway, SET CHECK_ROOT_INSTANCE_RUNNING=false and re run the command.</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> If you encounter this error, simply restart the Karaf container manually. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-8140">ENTESB-8140</a></em></span> Start level of hot deploy bundles is 80 by default</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> Starting in the Fuse 7.0 GA release, in the Apache Karaf container the start level of hot deployed bundles is 80 by default. This can cause problems for the hot deployed bundles, because there are many system bundles and features that have the same start level. To work around this problem and ensure that hot deployed bundles start reliably, edit the <code class="literal">etc/org.apache.felix.fileinstall-deploy.cfg</code> file and change the <code class="literal">felix.fileinstall.start.level</code> setting as follows: </p>
            <pre class="screen">felix.fileinstall.start.level = 90</pre>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-7664">ENTESB-7664</a></em></span> Installing framework-security feature kills karaf</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> The <code class="literal">framework-security</code> OSGi feature must be installed using the <code class="literal">--no-auto-refresh</code> option, otherwise this feature will shut down the Apache Karaf container. For example: </p>
            <pre class="screen">feature:install -v --no-auto-refresh framework-security</pre>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-fuse-eap">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.5.&nbsp;Fuse on JBoss EAP</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse on JBoss EAP has the following known issues: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/JBEAP-21929">JBEAP-21929</a></em></span> (7.4.z) org.infinispan.client.hotrod module is missing a dependency on org.infinispan.protostream</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
            <p class="simpara"> In Fuse 7.9, the Camel Infinispan (<code class="literal">camel-infinispan</code>) component does not work for Fuse on JBoss EAP, because JBoss EAP 7.4.0 is missing a dependency on <code class="literal">org.infinispan.protostream</code> (see also <a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-16186">ENTESB-16186</a>). If you get the following error when using the Camel Infinispan component in Fuse on JBoss EAP 7.4.0: </p>
            <pre class="screen">java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: org/infinispan/protostream/SerializationContextInitializer
    Caused by: java.lang.ClassNotFoundException: org.infinispan.protostream.SerializationContextInitializer from [Module \"org.infinispan.client.hotrod\" version 11.0.9.Final-redhat-00001 from local module loader</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> You can work around this problem by modifying <code class="literal">$EAP_HOME/modules/system/layers/base/org/infinispan/client/hotrod/main/module.xml</code>, adding the <code class="literal">org.infinispan.protostream</code> module as follows: </p>
            <pre class="screen">&lt;module name="org.infinispan.client.hotrod" xmlns="urn:jboss:module:1.x"&gt;
    &lt;properties&gt;
        &lt;property name="jboss.api" value="private"/&gt;
    &lt;/properties&gt;

    &lt;resources&gt;
        &lt;resource-root path="infinispan-client-hotrod-x.x.x.Final-redhat-00001.jar"/&gt;
    &lt;/resources&gt;

    &lt;dependencies&gt;
        &lt;module name="javax.api"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="javax.transaction.api"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="com.google.protobuf" optional="true"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="io.netty"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="org.infinispan.commons"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="org.jboss.logging"/&gt;
        &lt;module name="org.infinispan.protostream" optional="true"/&gt;  &lt;!-- add this line --&gt;
    &lt;/dependencies&gt;
&lt;/module&gt;</pre>
            <p class="simpara"> As this problem arises in the underlying JBoss EAP container, the problem could be solved by upgrading to a fixed (and supported) version of JBoss EAP as soon as a fix becomes available. </p>
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-13168">ENTESB-13168</a></em></span> Camel deployment on EAP domain mode is not working on Windows</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Starting in Fuse 7.6.0, for Fuse on JBoss EAP, the Camel subsystem cannot be deployed on JBoss EAP in domain mode on Windows OS. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-tooling">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.6.&nbsp;Fuse Tooling</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Fuse Tooling has the following known issue: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/FUSETOOLS-3460">FUSETOOLS-3460</a></em></span> Fuse Tooling temporarily uses deprecated templates</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             After CodeReady Studio 12.21 is released, Fuse Tooling will migrate from using the <code class="literal">fabric8-maven-plugin</code> to the <code class="literal">openshift-maven-plugin</code>. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term">_<a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/FUSETOOLS-3384">FUSETOOLS-3384</a>_Fuse Tooling temporarily uses Java 8</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             While Fuse Tooling currently works with Java 11, full support for the templates that use Java 11 will be provided with Fuse Tooling in the CodeReady Studio 12.21 release. 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section class="section" id="known-issues-camel">
         <div class="titlepage">
          <div>
           <div>
            <h2 class="title">7.7.&nbsp;Apache Camel</h2>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p> Apache Camel has the following known issues: </p>
         <div class="variablelist">
          <dl class="variablelist">
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.redhat.com/browse/ENTESB-15343">ENTESB-15343</a></em></span> XSLT component not working properly with IBM1.8 JDK</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             In Fuse 7.8, the Camel XSLT component does not work properly with the IBM 1.8 JDK. The problem occurs because the underlying Apache Xerces implementation of XSLT does not support the <code class="literal">javax.xml.XMLConstants#FEATURE_SECURE_PROCESSING</code> property (see <a class="link" href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/XERCESJ-1654">XERCESJ-1654</a>). 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-11060">ENTESB-11060</a></em></span> [camel-linkedin] V1 API is no longer supported</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.4.0, the Camel LinkedIn component is no longer able to communicate with the LinkedIn server, because it is implemented using the LinkedIn Version 1.0 API, which is no longer supported by LinkedIn. The Camel LinkedIn component will be updated to use the Version 2 API in a future release of Fuse. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-7469">ENTESB-7469</a></em></span> Camel Docker component cannot use Unix socket connections on EAP</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Since Fuse 7.0, the <code class="literal">camel-docker</code> component can connect to Docker only through its REST API, not through UNIX sockets. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-5231">ENTESB-5231</a></em></span> PHP script language does not work</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The PHP scripting language is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Camel applications on the Apache Karaf container, because there is no OSGi bundle available for PHP. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-5232">ENTESB-5232</a></em></span> Python language does not work</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             The Python scripting language is <span class="strong strong"><strong>not</strong></span> supported in Camel applications on the Apache Karaf container, because there is no OSGi bundle available for Python. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-2443">ENTESB-2443</a></em></span> Google Mail API - Sending of messages and drafts is not synchronous</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             When you send a message or draft, the response contains a Message object with an ID. It may not be possible to immediately get this message via another call to the API. You may have to wait and retry the call. 
           </dd>
           <dt>
            <span class="term"><span class="emphasis"><em><a class="link" href="https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ENTESB-2332">ENTESB-2332</a></em></span> Google Drive API JSON response for changes returns bad count of items for the first page</span>
           </dt>
           <dd>
             Google Drive API JSON response for changes returns bad count of items for the first page. Setting <code class="literal">maxResults</code> for a list operation may not return all the results in the first page. You may have to go through several pages to get the complete list (that is by setting <code class="literal">pageToken</code> on new requests). 
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </div>
        </section>
       </section>

  <script>
      'use strict';

            var $outerWrapper = document.querySelector('.pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer');
      if ($outerWrapper && $outerWrapper.closest) {
        var $containerWrapper = $outerWrapper.closest('.container');
        if ($containerWrapper) {
          $containerWrapper.classList.remove('container');
          $containerWrapper.classList.add('j-chrome-content-container');
        }
      }

            var cssRemoved = false;
      try {
        var $crapCss = document.querySelectorAll(
          'link[href*="/chrome_themes/nimbus/css/pages.css"], link[href*="/chrome_themes/nimbus/css/components.css"]'
        );
        if ($crapCss.length) {
          for (let index = 0; index < $crapCss.length; index++) {
            const $stylesheet = $crapCss[index];
            $stylesheet.remove();
          }
        }
        cssRemoved = true;
      }
      catch (error) {
        console.error('Ran into an issue while trying to retheme page', error);
        cssRemoved = false;
      }

            if (cssRemoved) {
        var $pvofOuterWrapper = document.querySelector('.pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer--css-not-removed');
        if ($pvofOuterWrapper) {
          $pvofOuterWrapper.classList.remove('pvof-doc__content-wrapper__outer--css-not-removed');
        }
      }
    </script>
